PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

, by Adam Lowisz on November 13, 2024, viewed 46,000 times said: "Pete Hegseth calls Putin a war criminal and says Biden has been a weak president.

The Ruling

!Needs Context <image:2704>

**Needs Context.**

Pete Hegseth did say Russian President Vladimir Putin was a "war criminal" during a broadcast on Fox News in March 2022, near the start of the invasion. spending supporting Ukraine, and downplayed Putin's aggression.

Think about it through the psychology of him."

The Facts

While Hegseth aligned with the claim that Putin was a "war criminal," the clip shared online was from March 2022 not long after the outbreak of the conflict.

Since then Hegseth has been more cautious, and critical of the U.S. spending on the conflict, claims appeared on social media repeating comments Hegseth had made criticizing Russian President [Vladimir Putin](https://www.newsweek.com/topic/vladimir-putin)
 in bold terms.

!Pete Hegseth <image:2703>

Pete Hegseth on May 31, 2019, in New York City. intervention in Ukraine and the prognosis from others that Russia's intervention would lead to wider conflict.

In an episode of the _Shawn Ryan Show_ Podcast from November 2024, Hegseth said he did not see Putin taking the world into a wider global or nuclear conflict, saying his gains would be incremental, part of what he called a "get my s\*\*\* back" conflict.

"I found it overinflated from the beginning this idea that Vladimir Putin's attack on Ukraine was going to lead to nuclear war or war across the continent," Hegseth said.

"I've always felt like it was from the beginning, like a couple days in, I like, this feels like the Putin's 'give me my s\*\*\* back' war.

"It kind of feels like \[Putin thought\] 'I feel like you've been pushing pretty hard, and we used to have the former Soviet Union, and we're pretty proud of that, and Ukraine was a part of it, and all these other... I think he probably knows enough to know that it's probably not going much further than Ukraine.

"And I don't think he's a suicidal maniac who's hell-bent on bringing in armageddon with nuclear warfare."

Elsewhere, he has also defended Trump's comment in 2022 calling Putin "very savvy" after the Russian president announced Moscow's recognition of the independence of [two self-proclaimed republics](https://www.newsweek.com/blinken-says-swift-response-needed-russia-recognizing-new-republics-1681212)
 in eastern Ukraine.

While the White House and the [EU](https://www.newsweek.com/topic/eu)
 described Putin's actions as a violation of international law and a pretext for an invasion, Trump said [Putin's move was "genius" and "very savvy."](https://www.newsweek.com/trump-calls-putin-moving-troops-ukraine-peacekeeping-genius-1681557)

Hegseth defended the comments saying that Trump was trying to tease the media for obsessing over the Russian leader

"Here's the reality, Vladimir Putin lives rent-free in the minds of our media, of the American media," Hegseth said.

"No organism, no entity has done more to spread Russian propaganda and to prop up the strawman that is Vladimir Putin than our very own media."

In a [Fox News](https://www.foxnews.com/video/6320895317112)
 interview in February 2023 with South Carolina [Republican](https://www.newsweek.com/topic/republican)
 Representative [Nancy Mace](https://www.newsweek.com/topic/nancy-mace)
, Hegseth criticized the number of times President [Joe Biden](https://www.newsweek.com/topic/joe-biden)
 had visited Ukraine compared to the southern border of the U.S., and the "billions spent in Ukraine" suggesting he was ignoring "our problems at home."

He also asked "what do we get out of" the billions the U.S."

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

## Valid Actions

   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

# Search Result
From [Source](https://www.pressenterprise.com/2020/05/01/heres-why-the-missiles-on-the-crashed-f-16-near-march-air-reserve-base-did-not-explode/): Found exact image on website with title: Here's why the missiles on the crashed F-16 near March Air Reserve ...
Content: "

![A U.S. Air Force file photo shows the Air National Guard F-16 Fighting Falcon that crashed near March Air Reserve Base on May 16, 2019. (Courtesy of U.S. Air Force)\
](data:image/webp;base64,UklGRiQAAABXRUJQVlA4IBgAAAAwAQCdASoBAAEAAwA0JaQAA3AA/v3AgAA= "RPE-L-F16CRASH-0424b-01")

A U.S. Air Force file photo shows the Air National Guard F-16 Fighting Falcon that crashed near March Air Reserve Base on May 16, 2019. (Courtesy of U.S. Air Force)

By [Brian Rokos](https://www.pressenterprise.com/author/brian-rokos/ "Posts by Brian Rokos")
 | [brokos@scng.com](mailto:brokos@scng.com)
 | The Press-Enterprise

UPDATED: May 1, 2020 at 4:45 PM PDT

! <image:2710>

An F-16 Fighting Falcon rests inside a warehouse near March Air Reserve Base after crashing on May 16, 2019. The missiles on board did not explode. The plane suffered a loss of hydraulic pressure, rendering the pilot unable to control the jet, the U.S. Air Force said April 23, 2020. (Courtesy of U.S. Air Force)

The U.S. Air Force has answered a questioned that burned in people‚Äôs minds as bystanders were hurriedly pushed back to safer locations several times and the 215 Freeway was closed after [the crash of an Air National Guard F-16 fighter jet](https://www.pressenterprise.com/2019/05/16/plane-crashes-near-march-air-reserve-base-215-freeway-shut-down/)
 near March Air Reserve Base in 2019:

Why didn‚Äôt the missiles aboard the Flying Falcon explode on impact?

The reason, the Air Force said this week, is that the ordnance attached to the F-16 during its intercept training mission were never armed.

‚ÄúAircraft flying this mission do fly with live ordnance. In order for the weapons to detonate, there are multiple conditions that must be met, including arming and launching of the weapon to complete the detonation sequences,‚Äù said Capt. Tisha J. Yates, an Air Force spokeswoman at Joint Base Langley-Eustis in Virginia.

The missiles were eventually removed from the jet as it sat in a warehouse on Opportunity Way near the Riverside-Moreno Valley border. They were trucked to nearby Ben Clark Training Center, [where they were destroyed in a controlled detonation](https://www.pressenterprise.com/2019/05/17/x-9/)
.

‚ÄúThe determination to move civilians away from the scene was a safety measure put in place by the incident commander on scene and in coordination with NORAD based on the hazards present until all munitions were secured,‚Äù Yates said in response to questions from this news organization, [which first reported the cause of the crash](https://www.pressenterprise.com/2020/04/23/hydraulic-failure-caused-f-16-to-crash-near-march-base-last-year-air-force-says/)
.

The F-16 was assigned to the 114th Fighter Wing at Joe Foss Field in South Dakota. The pilot was attached to the 144th Fighter Wing at March.

On May 16, 2019, the pilot was returning from the two-jet maneuvers about 120 miles east of March when he lost hydraulic pressure and therefore the ability to control the aircraft. At 3:39 p.m., after burning off fuel, he ejected about 250 feet off the ground less than a mile from the base. The pilot suffered minor injuries, as did about a dozen people in the warehouse where the plane crashed.

The Air Force concluded in its 22-page accident report that the $24 million jet lost the fluid from its two hydraulic tanks when two inlet check valves ‚Äî each less than an inch tall ‚Äî failed because they were improperly installed.

Each valve consists of a cap, screw threads, a retainer ring and an O-ring that collectively are referred to as a screw cap. That screw cap screws into the valve body. The retainer helps keep the O-ring in place. It is primarily the screw cap retainer and O-ring that prevent hydraulic fluid from leaking under high pressure.

The investigation determined that both screw caps were not properly screwed into the valve bodies. The retainers were found to be deformed, and portions of the O-rings were missing. As a result, hydraulic fluid leaked out through the threads between the screw caps and the valve bodies.

A suspected hydraulic leak had been noted in the jet in March 2019. A new flight-control system that had been overhauled months earlier was installed on March 28, and the plane flew 10 more missions without incident before the crash. The report concluded that the overhaul process lacked ‚Äúan effective procedure to identify improper installation of ISA check valves.‚Äù ISA stands for Integrated Servo Actuator, a flight-control system.

In the wake of the crash, the Air Force also said this week that it studied the overhaul process and found a problem with how the inlet check valve was assembled during overhauls, said Derek Kaufman, a civilian spokesman for the Air Force Materiel Command at Wright-Patterson Air Force Base in Ohio.

There are two approved configurations of the valves. The older configuration uses smaller Teflon backing rings, and newer configurations use larger rings. The team discovered the potential for installation of the wrong-size backing ring since both size rings were packaged side by side, Kaufman said.

As a result, the Air Force changed the process for assembling the valves during overhauls. It separated the installation and inspection steps on the work documentation and added a secondary quality check for just O-ring backing ring installation. And it inserted a ‚Äúquality stamp‚Äù of the entire process for the first six months after the changes to ensure proper training was accomplished.

The Air Force also inspected all of its inlet check valves and found three to be defective. Those were fixed, Kaufman said.

‚ÄúWe review the facts for any lessons that can be applied to maintenance processes and training to improve the safety and quality of systems we deliver to our warfighters,‚Äù he said.

Originally Published: May 1, 2020 at 4:44 PM PDT

* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

Audio of this article is brought to you by the Air & Space Forces Association, honoring and supporting our Airmen, Guardians, and their families. Find out more at afa.org

The improper installation of two parts caused an [F-16](/weapons/f-16/ "Learn more about the F-16 Fighting Falcon")
‚Äòs hydraulic system to fail, making the pilot [lose control and crash into a warehouse in May 2019](https://www.airforcemag.com/f-16-crashes-during-norad-training-in-california/)
 while flying back to March Air Reserve Base, Calif., Air Force investigators found.

The F-16 pilot successfully ejected before the Viper crashed into the civilian building. The aircraft was destroyed at a loss of $24.99 million, and caused about $3.9 million in damage to the warehouse, according to an Air Combat Command Accident Investigation Board report.

The F-16C, tail number 88-0477 from the South Dakota Air National Guard‚Äôs 114th Fighter Wing, was operated by a pilot from the California Air National Guard‚Äôs 144th Fighter Wing Detachment 1 at March for homeland defense missions. On May 16, 2019, the F-16C took off as part of a two-ship formation for an aerospace control alert training mission in a nearby military operating area.

The two F-16s flew one-versus-one tactical intercepts, low-level proficiency training, and local area familiarization. While flying near Palm Springs, the pilot began receiving cockpit warnings of a potential hydraulic system issue with gauges showing low pressure and began going through appropriate checklists, according to the report.

About 20 miles from base, the pilot deployed speed brakes and lowered the landing gear to burn more fuel and let the wingman visually inspect the aircraft. With the speed brakes and gear deployed and locked, the pilot did not yet declare an emergency, but continued the approach to March, the report states.

The aircraft then indicated further loss of pressure in both of its ‚ÄúA and B‚Äù systems, and the pilot consulted checklists for dual hydraulic failure. Once they got close to the base, the wingman landed first on one of the base‚Äôs runways, allowing the damaged F-16 to land on a runway with an arresting cable.

With both hydraulic systems failing, the pilot declared an emergency and turned on emergency power as a precaution before starting a straight-in approach to the runway. About one mile before touching down, at about 300 feet above ground level, the F-16 began to roll to the left without any pilot input. The pilot tried to maintain control, and counter the roll, but the aircraft rolled hard to the right in a way that was inconsistent with the pilot‚Äôs input.

After losing control of the aircraft, the pilot ejected. Immediately after punching out, the F-16 crashed into the warehouse, located across a major highway from the base. A photograph of the impact shows the F-16‚Äôs nose sheared off and wings largely removed in a pile of boxes and equipment. The pilot parachuted onto the runway overrun at the base, and was briefly hospitalized with minor injuries.

The Accident Investigation Board found that the cause of the mishap was two improperly installed hydraulic check valves in the aircraft‚Äôs right flaperon integrated survoactuator‚Äîa part that translates electrical commands to the movement of flight control surfaces. For both of the parts that failed, investigators found the same problem: the retainer on a screw cap had deformed, with fragments tearing away allowing fluid to leak.

‚ÄúThis condition allowed hydraulic fluid to leak from both systems resulting in decreased hydraulic pressure to move flight control surfaces,‚Äù the report said. ‚ÄúThe \[pilot\] set up to land as soon as possible, but the system had lost enough pressure on final approach to prevent the \[aircraft\] from sustaining controlled flight.‚Äù

Maintainers with the 144th Fighter Wing Detachment 1 installed the parts as part of unscheduled maintenance in March 2019 after a possible hydraulic leak was discovered. The parts went through operational checks with no discrepancies found, and the aircraft had flown 10 sorties for 16.3 hours before the crash. The AIB states that there was an inadequate overhaul process, which lacked an effective procedure to identify problems with the installation of the check valves.¬†

Content: "

![An F-16 Fighting Falcon rests inside a warehouse near March Air Reserve Base after crashing on May 16, 2019. The plane suffered a loss of hydraulic pressure, rendering the pilot unable to control the jet, the U.S. Air Force said April 23, 2020. (Courtesy of U.S. Air Force)\
](data:image/webp;base64,UklGRiQAAABXRUJQVlA4IBgAAAAwAQCdASoBAAEAAwA0JaQAA3AA/v3AgAA= "RPE-L-F16-0424-01-01")

An F-16 Fighting Falcon rests inside a warehouse near March Air Reserve Base after crashing on May 16, 2019. The plane suffered a loss of hydraulic pressure, rendering the pilot unable to control the jet, the U.S. Air Force said April 23, 2020. (Courtesy of U.S. Air Force)

By [Brian Rokos](https://www.sbsun.com/author/brian-rokos/ "Posts by Brian Rokos")
 | [brokos@scng.com](mailto:brokos@scng.com)
 | The Press-Enterprise

UPDATED: April 23, 2020 at 12:44 PM PDT

! <image:2712>

An inlet check valve from the F-16 Fighting Falcon that crashed near March Air Reserve Base on May 16, 2019, is shown during the investigation into the crash. The U.S. Air Force concluded that the valve was improperly installed, leading to a leak of hydraulic fuel that rendered the pilot unable to control the aircraft. (Courtesy of U.S. Air Force)

A loss of hydraulic pressure prevented the pilot of the Air National Guard‚Äôs F-16 [that crashed near March Air Reserve Base](https://www.pe.com/2019/05/16/plane-crashes-near-march-air-reserve-base-215-freeway-shut-down/)
 last year from controlling the jet, the U.S. Air Force says in a report.

The pilot ejected and parachuted onto a base runway on May 16, 2019, suffering minor injuries. The $24 million Fighting Falcon plummeted through the roof of a warehouse, destroying the jet and causing a small fire.

Twelve people in the warehouse were treated for exposure to the debris, the Cal Fire/Riverside County Fire Department said at the time.

The 22-page report, dated April 14, said two inlet-check valves were improperly installed, resulting in damage to them that caused hydraulic fuel to leak.

The valves were part of a flight-control system that was overhauled in January 2019 and installed in the jet after a possible hydraulic leak was discovered several months later.

‚ÄúThe evidence also indicated an inadequate overhaul process that lacked an effective procedure to identify improper installation of ISA check valves,‚Äù the report says.

The F-16 was one of two jets initially practicing 120 miles east of March, which sits on the Riverside-Moreno Valley border. The planes were returning to March when the one jet lost hydraulic pressure.

The pilot burned off fuel before ejecting, the report says.

The F-16 was assigned to the 114th Fighter Wing at Joe Foss Field in South Dakota and ran some missions for the 144th Fighter Wing at March.

_This story is developing. Please check back for updates._

Originally Published: April 23, 2020 at 12:32 PM PDT

CNN ¬†‚Äî¬†

A Ukrainian pilot was killed and his F-16 fighter jet crashed after Russia launched a huge aerial assault involving hundreds of drones and scores of missiles overnight, the Ukrainian military said on Sunday.

The airman, named as 1st Class Lt. Maksym Ustymenko by the Ukrainian air force, was the third F-16 pilot killed since the Ukrainians began flying the jets last summer, and his plane was the fourth F-16 Ukraine has lost since then.

The air force said Ustymenko ‚Äúdid everything he could to steer the aircraft away from a populated area, but he did not have time to eject.‚Äù

Ustymenko‚Äôs death is a major loss for Ukraine. Only a small number of the country‚Äôs top pilots have been trained to fly F-16s, the most advanced of Ukraine‚Äôs fighter jets. The training is highly specialized and takes months to complete.

Ukraine‚Äôs President Volodymyr Zelensky said Ustymenko destroyed seven targets before being killed, praising him and the Ukrainian air force for ‚Äúheroically protecting‚Äù the country‚Äôs skies.

Zelensky said Moscow launched 477 drones and 60 missiles towards six different locations overnight into Sunday ‚Äì one of Russia‚Äôs largest ever aerial assaults in terms of weapons deployed, according to a CNN tally.

![This residential building in Odesa was hit by a Russian drone on June 28, 2025.](https://media.cnn.com/api/v1/images/stellar/prod/gettyimages-2221742451.jpg?q=w_1110,c_fill)

This residential building in Odesa was hit by a Russian drone on June 28, 2025.

Deadly aerial attacks
---------------------

Russia has ramped up its [airborne attacks](https://www.cnn.com/2025/06/15/europe/russia-tactics-swarms-of-killer-drones-intl-cmd)
 against Ukraine in recent weeks, launching hundreds of drones and missiles nearly every night.

These assaults are not just bigger and more frequent; they are also more concentrated and executed in a way that makes them a lot more difficult to combat ‚Äì as they are flown at higher altitudes, out of reach of machine guns.

Zelensky said on Sunday that more than 114 missiles, over 1,270 drones, and nearly 1,100 glide bombs were launched by Russia against Ukraine just this week.

The Ukrainian leader pleaded with Kyiv‚Äôs Western allies to provide more aerial defenses for his country, saying Russia will continue to attack Ukraine for as long as it can.

‚ÄúThis war must be brought to an end ‚Äî pressure on the aggressor is needed, and so is protection. Protection from ballistic and other missiles, from drones, and from terror,‚Äù Zelensky said.

He added that Ukraine was ready to buy ‚ÄúAmerican systems‚Äù to strengthen its air defenses ‚Äì a clear call to US President Donald Trump and his administration to allow Ukraine to purchase the Patriot air defense systems.

[![ukr strike 1.jpg](https://media.cnn.com/api/v1/images/stellar/prod/ukr-strike-1.jpg?c=16x9&q=h_144,w_256,c_fill)\

Exile Nova Telegram\

Related article Russia‚Äôs summer offensive in Ukraine underwhelms ‚Äì but Kyiv won‚Äôt be celebrating](/2025/06/29/europe/russia-summer-offensive-kyiv-ukraine-intl)

The Patriots are widely considered to be among the best air defense systems. While there are other systems manufactured by some of Ukraine‚Äôs other allies, none can match the Patriots when it comes to protection against advanced hypersonic and ballistic missiles.

Ukraine is known to have roughly half a dozen of the [US-made Patriot air defense systems](https://www.cnn.com/2025/03/05/world/trump-cut-ukrainian-aid-patriot-missiles-intl)
, although the exact numbers and their locations are closely guarded secrets.

The Patriots play a crucial role in Ukraine‚Äôs air defense, protecting millions of civilians from Russian missiles. But Kyiv is at risk of running out of missiles for these systems, as Trump continues to threaten withdrawing US aid from Ukraine.

The Ukrainian air force said Sunday it had downed 211 drones and 38 missiles launched by Moscow overnight. Russian strikes were recorded in six locations with debris reported across eight locations, it added.

The Russian Ministry of Defense claimed the strikes targeted Ukraine‚Äôs ‚Äúmilitary-industrial complex facilities and oil refineries,‚Äù but the Ukrainians said civilian infrastructure objects were hit.

At least 11 people were injured, including two children, in a Russian attack in the city of Smila, in the central region of Cherkasy, local officials said in an update on Sunday.

Three nine-story buildings, private houses, and cars were significantly damaged in the shelling, as well as four educational institutions and a psychiatric hospital, Ihor Taburets, head of Cherkasy regional military administration, said.

Landmines question
------------------

Also on Sunday, Zelensky announced he signed a decree that would take Ukraine out of the Ottawa Treaty, the international agreement that bans the use of anti-personnel landmines.

A long-signalled move by Ukraine, the withdrawal still needs to be approved by Ukraine‚Äôs parliament. The US under the Biden Administration approved shipments of landmines to Ukraine last November.

Large swathes of Ukrainian land, especially along the frontlines in the east and in areas that were once occupied by Russia, are off limits to civilians because of the mines. Makeshift signs and barriers warning people not to enter are a common sight on the edges of fields and forests and near roads.

Ukraine‚Äôs Foreign Ministry said in a statement that the country ‚Äúhas made a difficult but necessary political decision‚Äù to withdraw from the Ottawa convention, saying the government was ‚Äúconvinced‚Äù it was necessary to do so.

At the start of this year, the pact had 165 member states ‚Äì although several major powers, including Russia, China, India, Pakistan and the United States, have never signed up to it.

Finland, Poland, Latvia, Estonia and Lithuania ‚Äì which all border Russia ‚Äì have also made moves to pull out of the treaty arguing they were essential for defense.

CNN‚Äôs Sophie Tanno contributed reporting.

## Evidence
### Evidence from `reverse_search`
The image in the claim (<image:22>) is of an F-16 fighter jet that crashed into a warehouse near March Air Reserve Base in May 2019. The crash was caused by improperly installed parts in the aircraft's hydraulic system, not by Russian forces. The pilot ejected and survived.

The articles discussing the crash were published by The Press-Enterprise ([Source](https://www.pressenterprise.com/2020/05/01/heres-why-the-missiles-on-the-crashed-f-16-near-march-air-reserve-base-did-not-explode/)), Air & Space Forces Magazine ([Source](https://www.airandspaceforces.com/improperly-installed-parts-caused-f-16-to-crash-into-warehouse-in-may-2019/)), and The Sun ([Source](https://www.sbsun.com/2020/04/23/hydraulic-failure-caused-f-16-to-crash-near-march-base-last-year-air-force-says/)). The articles include images of the wreckage (<image:2710>, <image:2711>) and the hydraulic system (<image:2712>).


### Evidence from `web_search`
CNN ([https://www.cnn.com/2025/06/29/europe/ukraine-f-16-pilot-killed-russia](https://www.cnn.com/2025/06/29/europe/ukraine-f-16-pilot-killed-russia)) and Reuters ([https://www.reuters.com/world/europe/ukraine-pilot-killed-f-16-fighter-jet-lost-ukrainian-military-says-2025-06-29/](https://www.reuters.com/world/europe/ukraine-pilot-killed-f-16-fighter-jet-lost-ukrainian-military-says-2025-06-29/)) report that a Ukrainian F-16 fighter jet was lost after a Russian attack, resulting in the death of the pilot.

ABC News ([https://abcnews.go.com/International/ukraine-loses-16-fighter-amid-massed-russian-drone/story?id=123315001](https://abcnews.go.com/International/ukraine-loses-16-fighter-amid-massed-russian-drone/story?id=123315001)) also reports the loss of a Ukrainian F-16 during an attempt to repel a Russian attack, mentioning that the pilot, Maksym Ustimenko, shot down seven targets before his F-16 was damaged. <image:4546>


# Your Analysis



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The claim is inaccurate. The image depicts an F-16 fighter jet that crashed in a warehouse near March Air Reserve Base in May 2019 due to mechanical failure, not a Russian attack. However, there is evidence of Ukrainian F-16s being lost in combat with Russia.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

On 6 August 2024, during the [Russian invasion of Ukraine](/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine")
,[\[36\]](#cite_note-dw.com-38)
[\[37\]](#cite_note-ft.com-39)
\[_[failed verification](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")\
 ‚Äì [see discussion](/wiki/Talk:Kursk_campaign#A_ridiculous_edit "Talk:Kursk campaign")\
_\] part of the [Russo-Ukrainian War](/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War "Russo-Ukrainian War")
, the [Armed Forces of Ukraine](/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Ukraine "Armed Forces of Ukraine")
 launched an incursion into [Russia](/wiki/Russia "Russia")
's [Kursk Oblast](/wiki/Kursk_Oblast "Kursk Oblast")
 and clashed with the [Russian Armed Forces](/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces "Russian Armed Forces")
 and [Russian border guard](/wiki/FSB_Border_Service_of_Russia "FSB Border Service of Russia")
.[\[38\]](#cite_note-REU86-40)
[\[36\]](#cite_note-dw.com-38)
[\[37\]](#cite_note-ft.com-39)
 A [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency_in_Russia "State of emergency in Russia")
 was declared in Kursk Oblast,[\[39\]](#cite_note-BBC_8_Aug-41)
 and Russian reserves were rushed to the area.[\[40\]](#cite_note-BBC_Cursino-42)
 By the end of the first week, the Ukrainian military said it had captured 1,000¬†km2 (390¬†sq¬†mi) of Russian territory, while Russian authorities acknowledged that Ukraine had captured 28 settlements.[\[41\]](#cite_note-43)

In the second half of August the front stabilized,[\[42\]](#cite_note-forbes_20240911-44)
 and in early October, the Ukrainian advance had stalled.[\[11\]](#cite_note-CNN_Third_Month-12)
 From November, North Korean forces were sent to the province to support the Russian military. By the end of August, the operation began to be criticized for diverting Ukrainian forces from [the east](/wiki/Eastern_Ukraine_campaign "Eastern Ukraine campaign")
, stretching Ukraine's personnel along the front and allowing Russia to [advance toward Pokrovsk](/wiki/Pokrovsk_offensive "Pokrovsk offensive")
.[\[46\]](#cite_note-AlexHorton-48)
[\[47\]](#cite_note-Miller-49)
 The [Institute for the Study of War](/wiki/Institute_for_the_Study_of_War "Institute for the Study of War")
 reported that Russia had moved forces from "lower-priority" areas, but not from Donetsk Oblast.[\[48\]](#cite_note-50)

The Ukrainian incursion into Kursk surprised Russia, some of Ukraine's allies, and many in the Ukrainian elite.[\[40\]](#cite_note-BBC_Cursino-42)
[\[49\]](#cite_note-ap_20240814-51)
[\[50\]](#cite_note-guardiansept-52)
 It is the most significant attack across the border since the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine,[\[51\]](#cite_note-53)
 and the first carried out primarily by Ukrainian regular forces. According to Russia, the incursion involved around 300 Ukrainian troops, 11 tanks, and over 20 [armored combat vehicles](/wiki/Armoured_fighting_vehicle "Armoured fighting vehicle")
,[\[67\]](#cite_note-MT86-69)
 and was aimed in two directions: at [Oleshnya](/wiki/Oleshnya,_Kursk_Oblast "Oleshnya, Kursk Oblast")
 in the direction of [Sudzha](/wiki/Sudzha "Sudzha")
, east-northeast of [Sumy](/wiki/Sumy "Sumy")
, and towards [Nikolayevo-Darino](/wiki/Nikolayevo-Darino "Nikolayevo-Darino")
, north-northeast of Sumy.[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)
 It was reported that Chechen [Akhmat battalions](/wiki/Russian_irregular_units_in_Ukraine#Akhmat_battalions "Russian irregular units in Ukraine")
 were responding to the raids,[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)
 though these claims remained unverified as of 13 September 2024.[\[69\]](#cite_note-71)

The attack began at 08:00 [MSK](/wiki/Moscow_Time "Moscow Time")
. [Alexei Smirnov](/wiki/Alexei_Smirnov_(politician) "Alexei Smirnov (politician)")
, acting [governor of Kursk Oblast](/wiki/Governor_of_Kursk_Oblast "Governor of Kursk Oblast")
, reported that three people died during the events: a woman in the border incursion and two individuals in separate drone attacks.[\[70\]](#cite_note-72)
 Russian [milbloggers](/wiki/Milblog "Milblog")
 also largely dismissed the supposed raids as "unsuccessful" and a "media stunt".[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)

According to Russia, at least 1,000 troops crossed the border on the first day, supported by [tanks](/wiki/Tank "Tank")
 and armored vehicles.[\[39\]](#cite_note-BBC_8_Aug-41)
 According to Andrzej Wilk of the [Centre for Eastern Studies](/wiki/Centre_for_Eastern_Studies "Centre for Eastern Studies")
, the entire Ukrainian grouping, including some elements which did not cross over into Russia, consisted of an estimated 2,000 men from Ukraine's [22nd](/wiki/22nd_Mechanized_Brigade_(Ukraine) "22nd Mechanized Brigade (Ukraine)")
 and [82nd](/wiki/82nd_Air_Assault_Brigade_(Ukraine) "82nd Air Assault Brigade (Ukraine)")
 Brigades, supported by artillery and air defense sub-units.[\[66\]](#cite_note-wilk-68)
 It was later claimed by members of the Ukrainian military that the breakthrough on the border was conducted by the 80th and 82nd Air Assault Brigades.[\[64\]](#cite_note-Kyrylenko-66)

Russian milbloggers claimed that the offensive was being performed by the [Russian Volunteer Corps](/wiki/Russian_Volunteer_Corps "Russian Volunteer Corps")
 (RVC), while the _[New Voice of Ukraine](/wiki/New_Voice_of_Ukraine "New Voice of Ukraine")
_ citing a source in [Ukraine's Main Military Intelligence](/wiki/Ukraine%27s_Main_Military_Intelligence "Ukraine's Main Military Intelligence")
 reported that the RVC was not present.[\[68\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg/250px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg)

#### 7 August

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg/250px-Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg)

1943 Ukrainian railway map shows Sudzha in quadrant A2 at km 60 on the [Lgov](/wiki/Lgov,_Kursk_Oblast "Lgov, Kursk Oblast")
‚Äì[Gotnya](/wiki/Gotnya "Gotnya")
‚Äì[Zolochiv](/wiki/Zolochiv,_Kharkiv_Oblast "Zolochiv, Kharkiv Oblast")
 main line to [Kharkiv](/wiki/Kharkiv "Kharkiv")

A milblogger claimed that Ukrainian forces had captured 11 settlements and had advanced 14 kilometres (9¬†mi) deep into the oblast.[\[71\]](#cite_note-NBC87-73)
 Government agencies were ordered by President [Vladimir Putin](/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")
 to "provide the needed assistance to residents", and deputy prime minister [Denis Manturov](/wiki/Denis_Manturov "Denis Manturov")
 was sent to oversee their work.[\[72\]](#cite_note-mt1-74)
 Kursk Oblast was placed under a [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency "State of emergency")
 by governor Smirnov.[\[73\]](#cite_note-dw1-75)
[\[74\]](#cite_note-CNBC_State_of_Emergency-76)

Putin met with key members of the security establishment including [Valery Gerasimov](/wiki/Valery_Gerasimov "Valery Gerasimov")
, [Alexander Bortnikov](/wiki/Alexander_Bortnikov "Alexander Bortnikov")
, [Sergei Shoigu](/wiki/Sergei_Shoigu "Sergei Shoigu")
 and [Andrey Belousov](/wiki/Andrey_Belousov "Andrey Belousov")
 on the Kursk incursion.[\[75\]](#cite_note-kru1-77)
 Gerasimov told Putin that about 1,000 Ukrainian soldiers took part in the attack and that their advance had been halted.[\[74\]](#cite_note-CNBC_State_of_Emergency-76)
[\[76\]](#cite_note-Reuters_Videos_show_Ukrainian_Presence-78)

Geolocated footage confirmed that Ukrainian forces had advanced at least 10 kilometres (6.2¬†mi) across the Russian border, having penetrated at least two Russian defensive lines and a stronghold. Additionally, there were reports of fighting in [Ivnitsa](/w/index.php?title=Ivnitsa&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ivnitsa (page does not exist)")
¬†\[[ru](https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%98%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_(%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C) "ru:–ò–≤–Ω–∏—Ü–∞ (–ö—É—Ä—Å–∫–∞—è –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å)")\

\], a village 24¬†km (15¬†mi) from the border.[\[79\]](#cite_note-Politico_August_8-81)
 Russian sources claimed that Ukrainian forces had reached the village of [Darino](/wiki/Darino,_Kursk_Oblast "Darino, Kursk Oblast")
.[\[80\]](#cite_note-82)

#### 8 August

[RIA Novosti](/wiki/RIA_Novosti "RIA Novosti")
 reported that four people died as a result of 'attacks' by the [AFU](/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Ukraine "Armed Forces of Ukraine")
 in the oblast[\[81\]](#cite_note-Rai_2024-08-08-2-83)
 as fighting continued for the third day.[\[82\]](#cite_note-Reuters_2024-08-08-84)
[\[83\]](#cite_note-AlJazeera_2024-08-08-85)
 Pro-Russian milblogger Yuri Podolyaka said that "Sudzha is basically lost to us" and that Ukrainian forces were pushing towards [Lgov](/wiki/Lgov,_Kursk_Oblast "Lgov, Kursk Oblast")
.[\[84\]](#cite_note-86)

Ukrainian forces were in control of the western part of Sudzha and the surrounding roads; skirmishes continued in the town.[\[85\]](#cite_note-agent-87)

According to Smirnov, the acting governor of Kursk Oblast, six Ukrainian drones and five missiles were shot down during the night and morning.[\[86\]](#cite_note-meduzalive8aug-88)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/President_Vladimir_Putin_talks_with_the_governor_of_Kursk_in_August_2024.jpg/250px-President_Vladimir_Putin_talks_with_the_governor_of_Kursk_in_August_2024.jpg)](/wiki/File:President_Vladimir_Putin_talks_with_the_governor_of_Kursk_in_August_2024.jpg)

[Vladimir Putin](/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")
 talks with [Alexei Smirnov](/wiki/Alexei_Smirnov_(politician) "Alexei Smirnov (politician)")
, the acting [governor of Kursk](/wiki/Governor_of_Kursk_Oblast "Governor of Kursk Oblast")
, about the situation regarding the Ukrainian incursion. As a result of the UAV attack, Kurchatov, as well as parts of the [Kurchatovsky](/wiki/Kurchatovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Kurchatovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
, [Oktyabrsky](/wiki/Oktyabrsky,_Lgovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Oktyabrsky, Lgovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
, [Bolshesoldatsky](/wiki/Bolshesoldatsky "Bolshesoldatsky")
, [Oboyansky](/wiki/Oboyansky "Oboyansky")
 and [Belovsky](/wiki/Belovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Belovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
 districts, were left without power supply.[\[105\]](#cite_note-107)

A counter-terrorism operational regime under the [Federal Security Service](/wiki/Federal_Security_Service "Federal Security Service")
, headed by [Alexander Bortnikov](/wiki/Alexander_Bortnikov "Alexander Bortnikov")
,[\[5\]](#cite_note-ISW_2024-08-10-6)
 was introduced in [Kursk](/wiki/Kursk_Oblast "Kursk Oblast")
, [Bryansk](/wiki/Bryansk_Oblast "Bryansk Oblast")
 and [Belgorod Oblasts](/wiki/Belgorod_Oblast "Belgorod Oblast")
 to temporarily take control of the regions till the conditions return to normalcy.[\[106\]](#cite_note-108)
 This meant that movement was restricted, vehicles could be seized, and phone calls could be monitored, among other measures.[\[107\]](#cite_note-voa1-109)

The number of Ukrainian troops in Kursk Oblast was estimated by [CEIP](/wiki/Carnegie_Endowment_for_International_Peace "Carnegie Endowment for International Peace")
 senior fellow Dara Massicot to be around 10,000‚Äì12,000, containing elements from four to five Ukrainian brigades.[\[108\]](#cite_note-110)

#### 10 August

According to analysts cited by _[The New York Times](/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times")
_, the Ukrainian advance in Kursk Oblast had largely been stopped by Russian reinforcements at this point, and the situation stabilized, but Ukrainian forces continued to hold on to their captured territory.[\[109\]](#cite_note-111)
 Conversely, other sources such as the _[Washington Post](/wiki/Washington_Post "Washington Post")
_ and _[Frankfurter Rundschau](/wiki/Frankfurter_Rundschau "Frankfurter Rundschau")
_ reported that Russia remained unable to control the situation, with continued Ukrainian advances.[\[110\]](#cite_note-Khurshudyan810-112)
[\[111\]](#cite_note-113)
 The [Russian Ministry of Defense](/wiki/Russian_Ministry_of_Defense "Russian Ministry of Defense")
 made similar claims that they had stopped any Ukrainian advances in Kursk Oblast.[\[112\]](#cite_note-114)
 Russian authorities introduced a "counter-terrorist operation" regime in Kursk Oblast.[\[113\]](#cite_note-115)
[\[107\]](#cite_note-voa1-109)

Battles were reported in [Olgovka](/wiki/Olgovka,_Kursk_Oblast "Olgovka, Kursk Oblast")
 near Korenevo, the Ivashkovskoye farmstead, and Malaya Loknya.[\[114\]](#cite_note-116)

On 10 August, Ukraine's [95th Air Assault Brigade](/wiki/95th_Air_Assault_Brigade "95th Air Assault Brigade")
 entered Kursk Oblast, and was given the task of conducting assaults and mop-up operations around [Malaya Loknya](/wiki/Malaya_Loknya "Malaya Loknya")
 and [Pogrebki](/w/index.php?title=Pogrebki&action=edit&redlink=1 "Pogrebki (page does not exist)")
¬†\[[ru](https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BA%D0%B8_(%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C) "ru:–ü–æ–≥—Ä–µ–±–∫–∏ (–ö—É—Ä—Å–∫–∞—è –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å)")\
\].[\[64\]](#cite_note-Kyrylenko-66)

The Russian Armed Forces claimed to have regained control of the village of Makhnovka east of Sudzha.[\[115\]](#cite_note-117)
 Reports claimed that the combat zone had expanded to 650¬†km2 (250¬†sq¬†mi).[\[116\]](#cite_note-118)

In the evening, Kursk Oblast governor Smirnov said that 15 people were injured in Kursk city after the wreckage of an intercepted Ukrainian missile fell onto a residential area.[\[117\]](#cite_note-BBC_Tough_Response-119)

Soldiers of Ukraine's [252nd Territorial Defense Battalion](/wiki/241st_Territorial_Defense_Brigade_(Ukraine) "241st Territorial Defense Brigade (Ukraine)")
 published footage from Poroz, a border village in [Belgorod Oblast](/wiki/Belgorod_Oblast "Belgorod Oblast")
.[\[110\]](#cite_note-Khurshudyan810-112)

#### 11 August

On the night of 11 August, the Ukrainian Armed Forces entered [Belovsky District](/wiki/Belovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Belovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
, located southeast of Sudzhansky District, which was confirmed by the head of the district and the acting governor. Russian officials said that the loss of the bridge would hinder the relocation via land routes of civilians in the district.[\[151\]](#cite_note-153)
[\[152\]](#cite_note-154)
 Approximately 2,000 to 3,000 Russian conscripts were trapped in a [pocket](/wiki/Pocket_(military) "Pocket (military)")
 south of the river.[\[153\]](#cite_note-155)

#### 17 August

Russian forces reportedly blew up two bridges near [Tyotkino](/wiki/Tyotkino "Tyotkino")
 and [Popovo-Lezhachi](/wiki/Popovo-Lezhachi "Popovo-Lezhachi")
 after withdrawing from the right bank of the [Seym River](/wiki/Seym_River "Seym River")
 in the area.[\[154\]](#cite_note-156)

The Ukrainian military claimed the capture of the settlement of [Korenevo](/wiki/Korenevo,_Korenevsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Korenevo, Korenevsky District, Kursk Oblast")
 but the Russian MOD described the settlement as contested.[\[155\]](#cite_note-157)

#### 18 August

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg/250px-The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg)

Ukrainian soldiers with a captured Russian [T-90](/wiki/T-90 "T-90")
M Proryv tank

Ukrainian forces destroyed another bridge over the [Seym](/wiki/Seym_(river) "Seym (river)")
 river near [Zvannoye](/wiki/Zvannoye "Zvannoye")
.[\[156\]](#cite_note-158)
[\[157\]](#cite_note-ISW_2024-08-16-159)
[\[158\]](#cite_note-160)

According to Russian bloggers, both Ukraine and Russia reinforced their forces battling in Kursk Oblast, with Russia moving some forces from other fronts to the front.[\[159\]](#cite_note-newsweek20240818-161)
\[_[better¬†source¬†needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")\
_\]

Marines from the [501st Separate Naval Infantry Battalion](/wiki/501st_Separate_Naval_Infantry_Battalion "501st Separate Naval Infantry Battalion")
 posted a video of them tearing down the Russian flag from the municipal building of [Apanasovka](/wiki/Apanasovka,_Korenevsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Apanasovka, Korenevsky District, Kursk Oblast")
.[\[160\]](#cite_note-162)

#### 19 August

Russia claimed that the Ukrainian military destroyed the third and last bridge over the Seym River in [Korenevsky District](/wiki/Korenevsky_District "Korenevsky District")
 leading to possible logistical strain on over 700 square kilometers of Russian territory.[\[161\]](#cite_note-163)

In his evening address, President Zelenskyy said that Ukrainian forces were in control of 92 settlements in Kursk Oblast and 1,250 square kilometers of Russian territory.[\[162\]](#cite_note-164)

#### 20 August

The Russian interior ministry warned residents of Bryansk, Kursk and Belgorod Oblasts against using online dating websites and security cameras, citing concerns of information being gathered by Ukrainian forces.[\[163\]](#cite_note-165)
 [Yunus-Bek Yevkurov](/wiki/Yunus-Bek_Yevkurov "Yunus-Bek Yevkurov")
, former head of [Ingushetia](/wiki/Ingushetia "Ingushetia")
 and incumbent deputy head of the Ministry of Defense was appointed as [Andrei Belousov](/wiki/Andrei_Belousov "Andrei Belousov")
's deputy in the Coordinating Council for the Security Issues of the Bordering Territories. The ministry stated, "After suffering losses, the Ukrainian sabotage group retreated to its territory, while some of the fighters attempted to establish a position on the territory adjacent to the state border, where they were blocked by Russian army units."[\[298\]](#cite_note-nva-300)
[\[299\]](#cite_note-guardian-301)
 President [Vladimir Putin](/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")
 described the AFU's offensive into Kursk Oblast as a "large-scale provocation." He accused the "Kyiv regime" of "indiscriminately firing various types of weapons, including missiles, at civilian buildings, houses, and ambulances." Putin stated that he plans to meet with the heads of the security agencies, the Defense Ministry, and the [Federal Security Service](/wiki/Federal_Security_Service "Federal Security Service")
 (FSB).[\[71\]](#cite_note-NBC87-73)
[\[16\]](#cite_note-surface-17)

[State Duma](/wiki/State_Duma "State Duma")
 deputy and retired major general [Andrey Gurulyov](/wiki/Andrey_Gurulyov "Andrey Gurulyov")
 criticized the Russian army for failing to defend Kursk Oblast.[\[300\]](#cite_note-302)
 On 8 August, Gurulyov said in a television interview that the Russian military knew about the planned Ukrainian invasion of Kursk a month before it happened but "from the top came the order not to panic, and that those above know better."[\[301\]](#cite_note-303)

On 13 August, an immediate special meeting in the "[Arria format](/wiki/Arria_format "Arria format")
" of the [United Nations Security Council](/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council "United Nations Security Council")
 took place on request of Russia's Commissioner for Human Rights [Tatyana Moskalkova](/wiki/Tatyana_Moskalkova "Tatyana Moskalkova")
, who demanded to "condemn the actions of Ukraine" in relation to the events in Kursk Oblast.[\[302\]](#cite_note-304)

In response to the offensive, Putin has reportedly set deadlines for Russian forces to push Ukrainian troops out of Kursk Oblast, first by October 2024, which was then delayed to January 2025.[\[303\]](#cite_note-y851-305)
[\[304\]](#cite_note-g362-306)

Pro-Kremlin political analyst [Sergei Markov](/wiki/Sergei_Markov "Sergei Markov")
 told _The Washington Post_ that "the signal came from intelligence to the leadership, but ... She said that Ukraine would be conducting humanitarian operations in the area, that international humanitarian organizations would be allowed to enter, and that [safe corridors](/wiki/Humanitarian_corridor "Humanitarian corridor")
 would be opened for civilians to evacuate toward Ukraine or to other parts of Russia.[\[330\]](#cite_note-332)

On 7 September, [Kyrylo Budanov](/wiki/Kyrylo_Budanov "Kyrylo Budanov")
 noted that the offensive into Kursk had impacted and "complicated" Russian plans for an offensive in the upcoming winter.[\[331\]](#cite_note-ISW_September_7-333)

On 13 September, Zelenskyy acknowledged the Russian counter-attack but claimed there had been "no serious (Russian) success", adding that "It gave the results that, frankly speaking, we counted on" and reiterated claims that it had adversely affected Russian operations in Kharkiv and Donetsk Oblasts.[\[332\]](#cite_note-334)
[\[333\]](#cite_note-335)
[\[187\]](#cite_note-ISW_2024_09_13-189)

On 16 September, the Ukrainian government invited the United Nations and the [International Committee of the Red Cross](/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross "International Committee of the Red Cross")
 to inspect areas of Kursk Oblast that were under its control.[\[334\]](#cite_note-336)

### United States

The [White House](/wiki/White_House "White House")
 said that it was seeking an understanding from Ukraine regarding the incursion, adding that it had no advance knowledge of the attack.[\[52\]](#cite_note-Al_Jazeera_Third_Day-54)
 On 8 August, Deputy Pentagon Press Secretary [Sabrina Singh](/wiki/Sabrina_Singh "Sabrina Singh")
 stated that the incursion is consistent with the US policy on the use of weapons.[\[335\]](#cite_note-politico_20240809-337)
 On 12 August, [US National Security Council](/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council "United States National Security Council")
 spokesperson [John Kirby](/wiki/John_Kirby_(admiral) "John Kirby (admiral)")
 called on Putin to withdraw his forces from Ukraine if he "doesn't like" the Ukrainian incursion in Kursk Oblast.[\[336\]](#cite_note-338)
 On 13 August, President [Joe Biden](/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden")
 said that the Ukrainian incursion was "creating a real dilemma" for Putin.[\[337\]](#cite_note-339)

### Germany

In response to the Kursk offensive, the German Foreign Ministry stated on 9 August that weapons transferred from Germany to Ukraine become the property of Ukraine and can be used by its armed forces as they deem necessary and correct."

From [Source](https://www.newsweek.com/russia-protests-american-soldiers-kursk-1942273): 
Content: "GAVRIIL GRIGOROV/POOL/AFP/Getty Images

Experts told _Newsweek_ that, even if an American PMC were operational in Kursk, it would not equate to Ukraine's raid being conducted under the direction or patronage of the Biden administration, as alleged by the Foreign Ministry.

Helene Olsen, a lecturer in defense studies at King's College London and an expert in the usa of mercenaries and other forms of private contractors in conflict, told _Newsweek_ that it is in the nature of PMCs to "go where the money is."

"While American PMCs traditionally have worked closely with the US Gov and many American PMCs have interests that align with the US Gov, PMCs, irrespective of origin, are ultimately businesses," Olsen said, adding that Russia "would benefit from making up these allegations considering the stigma connected with the private military industry."

Despite Russia's claims to the contrary, the U.S. Russia's President Vladimir Putin chairs a meeting regarding the situation in the Kursk region, in his residence in Novo-Ogaryovo outside Moscow, on August 12, 2024. More Evgeniy Maloletka/Associated Press

Eugenio Cusumano, associate professor of political science at the University of Messina, Italy, believes that Russia's allegations of American PMC presence in Kursk is "rather unlikely."

"Russia has repeatedly stated [NATO](https://www.newsweek.com/topic/nato)
 soldiers were fighting in Ukraine, German tanks with German crews were captured, a NATO biolab was found under Mariupol, all with no evidence," Cusumano told _Newsweek_.

Even if proven true, he added that the "the scale and impact of US contractors' involvement is most likely minimal," and that the presence of "a private firm serving private objectives" would not constitute America's direct involvement in Kursk.

Keir Giles, senior research fellow at Chatham House's Russia & Eurasia Program, was less skeptical of the Foreign Ministry's claim, given that "large numbers of foreign volunteers are fighting alongside and supporting Ukrainian forces, Americans among them."

However, Giles agreed that PMCs acting under the direction of the U.S. News Reporter

*   Russian Foreign Ministry summons US Charge d'affaires in Moscow Stephanie Holmes to convey strong protest against 'provocative actions of American reporters' and 'participation of the American PMCs'¬† ¬†

**MOSCOW**¬†

Russia protested on Tuesday that US private military companies (PMCs) are fighting alongside Ukraine in the Kursk region, while reporters from several major American media outlets illegally entered Russian territory to cover the incursion.¬†

The Russian Foreign Ministry claimed in a statement that soldiers from US private military companies are fighting alongside Ukrainian troops in the Kursk region, and journalists illegally entered Russian territory to cover the incursion.

US Charge d'affaires Stephanie Holmes was summoned to the Foreign Ministry in Moscow to convey strong protest against the "provocative actions of American reporters" and "participation of the American PMCs on the side of Ukraine's armed forces during their invasion" of Russia, it said.

"Such actions are contradicting statements by Joe Biden administration about non-involvement in Ukraine's neo-Nazi attack against Russia, proving with all clarity US involvement as a direct participant of the conflict in (Ukraine's President Volodymyr) Zelenskyy's malicious intentions," the ministry stressed.

The ministry warned that Russian law enforcement will investigate US citizens‚Äô actions and take necessary measures to bring them to justice.

"All foreign 'specialists' and mercenaries illegally crossing the border of our country automatically become a legitimate military target for the armed forces of the Russian Federation," it said.

 –≤ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ –æ–∫–∫—É–ø–∞–Ω—Ç—ã –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è–ª–∏ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ –∂–∏–≤–æ–π —Å–∏–ª—ã –∏ —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏.

# Your Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The search result from Apostrophe.ua, published on September 8, 2022, discusses the retreat of Russian forces from Balakleya in the Kharkiv region. It includes a photo of Ukrainian soldiers and mentions significant losses of Russian forces. SummarizeResultPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

# Example 1
The search result from America Today provides several photographs of the Notre-Dame Cathedral fire on April 15, 2019. <image:i>, <image:j>, <image:k>. None of the images show the Eiffel Tower in the background. 

# Example 2
NONE

# Example 3
The Guardian discusses a report blaming the Syrian government for a toxic gas attack and condemning their use of chemical weapons. The Guardian mentions the Chemical Weapons Convention and the responsibilities of Syria under the convention. According to The Guardian, The White House condemned the Assad regime for defying the norm against chemical weapons use.

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

# Example 1
The search result from America Today provides several photographs of the Notre-Dame Cathedral fire on April 15, 2019. <image:i>, <image:j>, <image:k>. None of the images show the Eiffel Tower in the background. 

# Example 2
NONE

# Example 3
The Guardian discusses a report blaming the Syrian government for a toxic gas attack and condemning their use of chemical weapons. The Guardian mentions the Chemical Weapons Convention and the responsibilities of Syria under the convention. According to The Guardian, The White House condemned the Assad regime for defying the norm against chemical weapons use.

–ò–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ –ë–∞–ª–∞–∫–ª–µ–∏ –ø–æ–∑–≤–æ–ª–∏–ª–æ –í–°–£ –ª–∏—à–∏—Ç—å —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫—É—é –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫—É, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è —Ç–∞–º —Å–∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ–Ω—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∞, –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞—Ç—å –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—É, –ø–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞–ª–æ –∏—Ö –æ—Ç ¬´–ª–æ–≥–∏—Å—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∏¬ª –í–æ–ª—á–∞–Ω—Å–∫-–ë–æ–ª—å—à–æ–π –ë—É—Ä–ª—É–∫-–ö—É–ø—è–Ω—Å–∫-–ò–∑—é–º, –ø–æ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–π –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏–ª–æ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏, –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç. ¬´–ë–µ–∑ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è –≤—Å—è —ç—Ç–∞ –º–∞—Å—Å–∞ –ª–∏—á–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∞ –∏ —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏, —Å–∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ–Ω—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–∞—è –Ω–∞ –ò–∑—é–º—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏, –æ–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∞—Å—å –±—ã –Ω–µ –±–æ–µ—Å–ø–æ—Å–æ–±–Ω–æ–π¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ.

–ü–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–≥–æ —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç–∞ –Æ—Ä–∏—è –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤–∞, —É —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–π—Å–∫ –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ ¬´–æ—á–µ–Ω—å –∫—Ä—É–ø–Ω—ã–µ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏¬ª: –Ω–µ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —É–±–∏—Ç—ã–º–∏, –Ω–æ –∏ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏: ¬´–∫–∞–∫ –º–∏–Ω–∏–º—É–º —Å–æ—Ç–Ω–∏ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö, –µ—Å–ª–∏ –Ω–µ –ø–∞—Ä–∞ —Ç—ã—Å—è—á¬ª.

–í–µ—Ä–æ—è—Ç–Ω–æ–µ –±–æ–ª—å—à–æ–µ –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞—é—Ç –∏ –¥–≤–æ–µ –±—ã–≤—à–∏—Ö –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏—Ö —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏. ¬´–ü—Ä–∏ —Å–ø–æ–Ω—Ç–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º –æ—Ç—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –æ—Å–æ–±–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö. –°–≤—è–∑–∏ –≤–Ω—É—Ç—Ä–∏ –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –Ω–µ—Ç. –ö—Ç–æ –≥–¥–µ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è, –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–∏—Ä—ã –Ω–µ –≤—Å–µ–≥–¥–∞ –∑–Ω–∞—é—Ç. –°–æ–æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–æ, –æ–± –æ—Ç—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –Ω–µ –≤—Å–µ –º–æ–≥—É—Ç –∑–Ω–∞—Ç—å¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä—è—Ç –æ–Ω–∏. –ë—ã–≤—à–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏–π –æ–¥–Ω–æ–≥–æ –∏–∑ —ç–ª–∏—Ç–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –≤ —Ä–∞–∑–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–µ —Å ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã–º–∏ –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏—è–º–∏¬ª –æ—Ç–º–µ—Ç–∏–ª, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –æ–±–µ —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã –Ω–µ—Å—É—Ç –æ—â—É—Ç–∏–º—ã–µ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏. ¬´–ö–æ–≥–¥–∞ –º–æ–∏ –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä—è—Ç: ‚Äû–ë–ª—è, —Ç–∞–º –ø–∏–∑–¥–µ—Ü‚Äú, –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –≤—Å—ë –ø–ª–æ—Ö–æ¬ª, ‚Äî –¥–æ–±–∞–≤–∏–ª —Å–æ–±–µ—Å–µ–¥–Ω–∏–∫ ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã—Ö –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏–π¬ª.
